--- Commit Message ---
LU-12916 osd: use writeback for small writes in ldiskfs

This patch implements the writeback caching for small writes on
Lustre OSD (ldiskfs).
The writes are not synchronous any more on OST. It marks the page
as dirty and create buffer heads mapping pages to the physical
blocks. The kernel writeback mechanism will handle the actual I/O.

This patch should improve the performance for I/O cases such as
small writes from many files (i.e. mdtest-hard-write) or
unaligned I/O on a shared file (i.e. ior-hard-write).

Add a ldiskfs patch "ext4-writeback.patch" to not zero out
non-full page during writeback for a encrypted file. Without this
ldiskfs patch, it will fail sanity-sec/test_37.

According to the benchmark results, this patch can improve the
IO500 mdtest-hard performance and the performance of the real
application Nek5000 turbulent pipe with more than 10%.

Signed-off-by: Alex Zhuravlev <bzzz@whamcloud.com>
Signed-off-by: Qian Yingjin <qian@ddn.com>
Change-Id: I9b5aa568a49d5b39d04656fdacb94c3a6ec5a7ff

--- Message (Alex Zhuravlev, 2023-04-19 08:29:24.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

> I/O cases such small writes from massive files

How is LDLM locking handled for this?  Is it handled?

--- Message (Qian Yingjin, 2023-08-03 02:26:00.000000000) ---

--- Message (Qian Yingjin, 2023-08-03 02:28:16.000000000) ---
Patch Set 41:

sorry, wrong answer. I thought you are commenting on batch small write.
we are improving in OSD layer. the LDLM locking is on OFD (target) layer. So the LDLM extent lock is already taken.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2023-08-03 13:24:46.000000000) ---
Patch Set 41:

How do you ensure it’s held?  Normally on the server it is dropped once the operation is complete, are you just not completing the write?  Or ?

--- Message (Qian Yingjin, 2023-08-03 14:21:15.000000000) ---
Patch Set 41:

(1 comment)

--- Message (Qian Yingjin, 2023-08-03 15:27:37.000000000) ---
Patch Set 41:

See https://review.whamcloud.com/#/c/fs/lustre-release/+/50687/1/lustre/osd-ldiskfs/osd_io.c@1172 for details.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2023-08-03 17:14:16.000000000) ---
Patch Set 41:

OK, I think I follow - locking is not necessary for the cache because the server stays the final source of truth, and all IO requests still use locks.  The server never generates new IO, so it doesn't need locking, because all IO ends in the write back cache anyway.  It just sits in front of the disk on the same node.

There are some complexities around how we handle IO safety since data in cache isn't on disk, but that's a separate issue from whether or not the cache uses locks.

That handles a concern Andreas raised in passing the other day.  Thanks.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-09-30 08:20:01.000000000) ---
Patch Set 42:

(1 comment)

If a large write overlaps with previous cache writes, does the cache in that range get flushed/invalidated before the large direct write is submitted?  Otherwise, it would be possible for the large direct write to be written to the file, then the old cached data written on top of it. 

It would be useful to test this with fsx with a range of IO sizes to confirm this is working correctly.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-10-01 02:59:25.000000000) ---
Patch Set 42:

(4 comments)

Alex, it would be useful to get your input on the latest version of this patch. 

I understand your earlier comments about CPU overhead for bufferheads for large writes, but this patch is focused on only caching small writes < 64KiB in size, where the read-modify-write of partial blocks dominates the overhead, and not the CPU cost of adding bufferheads to each page. 

The ior-hard-write benchmark is writing interleaved 47008-byte chunks from many threads into a single file, and this reflects a common HPC IO workload where many MPI ranks are writing out their data structures to a shared file in an unaligned way instead of writing a separate file for each MPI rank (to avoid creating 10M separate 47008-byte files).

Being able to cache this in OST RAM and aggregate the client writes into a single large write to disk can improve the performance significantly.  Yingjin, could you email the results from your FAST paper with Alex to show what gains are possible here...

--- Message (Qian Yingjin, 2023-10-25 01:53:02.000000000) ---
Patch Set 42:

This is for testonly right now...
For overlapping regions between buffered I/O and direct I/O:
On the client, overlapping regions are detected so that the dirty pages of this region must be completely flushed first before direct I/O can be performed. On the server side, with write-back enabled, dirty pages are not flushed and are reused instead as part of the direct I/O operation.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2023-10-25 02:42:18.000000000) ---
Patch Set 42:

> Patch Set 42:
> 
> This is for testonly right now...
> For overlapping regions between buffered I/O and direct I/O:
> On the client, overlapping regions are detected so that the dirty pages of this region must be completely flushed first before direct I/O can be performed. On the server side, with write-back enabled, dirty pages are not flushed and are reused instead as part of the direct I/O operation.

This sounds good, but also - if it is hard, it is probably not needed.  Mixed direct and buffered IO writes to the same pages is NOT a normal thing, so it doesn't have to be fast.  I guess there is the transition to DIO with hybrid + contention but that's still just a momentary thing.

Patch Set 67:

I attempted to fix the build errors present in this patch and succeeded. Yay! Now, keep in mind I barely have any idea what I am doing, so please doublecheck the changes I made to make sure they make sense.

This service is only provided in hopes to be useful and reduce latency from push to getting actual results in the face of trivial code errors

Here's summary of my changes:
The change in this patch fixes a compile error by correcting the argument passed to `ldiskfs_journal_stop()`.

### Summary of Changes:
- **Problem**: The original code passed `handle` to `ldiskfs_journal_stop()`, but the correct parameter should be `hdl` (the transaction handle stored in the `osd_handle` structure).
- **Fix**: Changed `ldiskfs_journal_stop(handle)` to `ldiskfs_journal_stop(hdl)`.

### Why it was necessary:
- `handle` was likely undefined or not the correct type in this context, causing a compile error.
- `hdl` (from `struct osd_handle *hdl`) is the proper transaction handle used in the `osd_handler.c` code path.
- This correction ensures the function call matches the expected API and resolves the compilation failure introduced in a prior patch.

### Impact:
- Fixes a compile-time error.
- Ensures proper transaction cleanup in the `osd_trans_stop` function.
- Maintains correctness of the journaling logic in the Lustre `osd-ldiskfs` layer.

Patch Set 70:

I attempted to fix the build errors present in this patch and succeeded. Yay! Now, keep in mind I barely have any idea what I am doing, so please doublecheck the changes I made to make sure they make sense.

This service is only provided in hopes to be useful and reduce latency from push to getting actual results in the face of trivial code errors

Here's summary of my changes:
Perfect! Now I can see that the `error` variable is properly defined in the `dio_complete_routine` function. The fix I applied should resolve the compilation error.

## Summary

**The Fix:**

The compile error was caused by the `osd_bio_fini` function using an undeclared `error` variable. The patch had moved code from `dio_complete_routine` into `osd_bio_fini` but didn't properly handle the `error` parameter.

**What I fixed:**

1. **Modified the function signature** of `osd_bio_fini` to accept an `error` parameter:
   ```c
   void osd_bio_fini(struct bio *bio, int error)
   ```

2. **Updated the function declaration** in `lustre/osd-ldiskfs/osd_internal.h` to match the new signature.

3. **Updated all calls** to `osd_bio_fini` to pass the error parameter:
   - In `dio_complete_routine`: `osd_bio_fini(bio, error);`
   - In `osd_bio_integrity_verify_fn`: `osd_bio_fini(bio, blk_status_to_errno(bio->bi_status));`

**Rationale:**

The original code in `dio_complete_routine` had access to the `error` variable (either passed as a parameter or extracted from `bio->bi_status` depending on kernel version). When the patch moved some of this functionality into `osd_bio_fini`, it needed to pass the error information along. This is consistent with C89 variable declaration requirements and maintains the original functionality where error handling depends on the error status of the bio operation.

The fix ensures that:
- The error status is properly propagated to the `osd_bio_fini` function
- The function can properly handle both read and write completion scenarios
- The error information is available for setting `iobuf->dr_error` when needed
